    1994             :  * a memory array.  No assumption is made that the words being swapped are
    1995             :  * word aligned in memory.  Use the CPL_LSB and CPL_MSB macros from cpl_port.h
    1996             :  * to determine if the current platform is big endian or little endian.  Use
    1997             :  * The macros like CPL_SWAP32() to byte swap single values without the overhead
    1998             :  * of a function call.

    3288             : /************************************************************************/
    3289             : /*                          GDALCopyWords64()                           */
    3290             : /************************************************************************/
    3291             : 
    3292             : /**
    3293             :  * Copy pixel words from buffer to buffer.
    3294             :  *
    3295             :  * This function is used to copy pixel word values from one memory buffer
    3296             :  * to another, with support for conversion between data types, and differing
    3297             :  * step factors. The data type conversion is done using the following
    3298             :  * rules:
    3299             :  * <ul>
    3300             :  * <li>Values assigned to a lower range integer type are clipped. For
    3301             :  * instance assigning GDT_Int16 values to a GDT_Byte buffer will cause values
    3302             :  * less the 0 to be set to 0, and values larger than 255 to be set to 255.
    3303             :  * </li>
    3304             :  * <li>
    3305             :  * Assignment from floating point to integer rounds to closest integer.
    3306             :  * +Infinity is mapped to the largest integer. -Infinity is mapped to the
    3307             :  * smallest integer. NaN is mapped to 0.
    3308             :  * </li>
    3309             :  * <li>
    3310             :  * Assignment from non-complex to complex will result in the imaginary part
    3311             :  * being set to zero on output.
    3312             :  * </li>
    3313             :  * <li> Assignment from complex to
    3314             :  * non-complex will result in the complex portion being lost and the real
    3315             :  * component being preserved (<i>not magnitude!</i>).
    3316             :  * </li>
    3317             :  * </ul>
    3318             :  *
    3319             :  * No assumptions are made about the source or destination words occurring
    3320             :  * on word boundaries.  It is assumed that all values are in native machine
    3321             :  * byte order.
    3322             :  *
    3323             :  * @param pSrcData Pointer to source data to be converted.
    3324             :  * @param eSrcType the source data type (see GDALDataType enum)
    3325             :  * @param nSrcPixelStride Source pixel stride (i.e. distance between 2 words),
    3326             :  * in bytes
    3327             :  * @param pDstData Pointer to buffer where destination data should go
    3328             :  * @param eDstType the destination data type (see GDALDataType enum)
    3329             :  * @param nDstPixelStride Destination pixel stride (i.e. distance between 2
    3330             :  * words), in bytes
    3331             :  * @param nWordCount number of words to be copied
    3332             :  *
    3333             :  * @note
    3334             :  * When adding a new data type to GDAL, you must do the following to
    3335             :  * support it properly within the GDALCopyWords function:
    3336             :  * 1. Add the data type to the switch on eSrcType in GDALCopyWords.
    3337             :  *    This should invoke the appropriate GDALCopyWordsFromT wrapper.
    3338             :  * 2. Add the data type to the switch on eDstType in GDALCopyWordsFromT.
    3339             :  *    This should call the appropriate GDALCopyWordsT template.
    3340             :  * 3. If appropriate, overload the appropriate CopyWord template in the
    3341             :  *    above namespace. This will ensure that any conversion issues are
    3342             :  *    handled (cases like the float -> int32 case, where the min/max)
    3343             :  *    values are subject to roundoff error.
    3344             :  */
    3345             :

    3537             : /************************************************************************/
    3538             : /*                            GDALCopyBits()                            */
    3539             : /************************************************************************/
    3540             : 
    3541             : /**
    3542             :  * Bitwise word copying.
    3543             :  *
    3544             :  * A function for moving sets of partial bytes around.  Loosely
    3545             :  * speaking this is a bitwise analog to GDALCopyWords().
    3546             :  *
    3547             :  * It copies nStepCount "words" where each word is nBitCount bits long.
    3548             :  * The nSrcStep and nDstStep are the number of bits from the start of one
    3549             :  * word to the next (same as nBitCount if they are packed).  The nSrcOffset
    3550             :  * and nDstOffset are the offset into the source and destination buffers
    3551             :  * to start at, also measured in bits.
    3552             :  *
    3553             :  * All bit offsets are assumed to start from the high order bit in a byte
    3554             :  * (i.e. most significant bit first).  Currently this function is not very
    3555             :  * optimized, but it may be improved for some common cases in the future
    3556             :  * as needed.
    3557             :  *
    3558             :  * @param pabySrcData the source data buffer.
    3559             :  * @param nSrcOffset the offset (in bits) in pabySrcData to the start of the
    3560             :  * first word to copy.
    3561             :  * @param nSrcStep the offset in bits from the start one source word to the
    3562             :  * start of the next.
    3563             :  * @param pabyDstData the destination data buffer.
    3564             :  * @param nDstOffset the offset (in bits) in pabyDstData to the start of the
    3565             :  * first word to copy over.
    3566             :  * @param nDstStep the offset in bits from the start one word to the
    3567             :  * start of the next.
    3568             :  * @param nBitCount the number of bits in a word to be copied.
    3569             :  * @param nStepCount the number of words to copy.
    3570             :  */
    3571             : 
    3572           0 : void GDALCopyBits(const GByte *pabySrcData, int nSrcOffset, int nSrcStep,
    3573             :                   GByte *pabyDstData, int nDstOffset, int nDstStep,
    3574             :                   int nBitCount, int nStepCount)
    3575             : 
    3576             : {
    3577           0 :     VALIDATE_POINTER0(pabySrcData, "GDALCopyBits");
    3578             : 
    3579           0 :     for (int iStep = 0; iStep < nStepCount; iStep++)
    3580             :     {
    3581           0 :         for (int iBit = 0; iBit < nBitCount; iBit++)
    3582             :         {
    3583           0 :             if (pabySrcData[nSrcOffset >> 3] & (0x80 >> (nSrcOffset & 7)))
    3584           0 :                 pabyDstData[nDstOffset >> 3] |= (0x80 >> (nDstOffset & 7));
    3585             :             else
    3586           0 :                 pabyDstData[nDstOffset >> 3] &= ~(0x80 >> (nDstOffset & 7));
    3587             : 
    3588           0 :             nSrcOffset++;
    3589           0 :             nDstOffset++;
    3590             :         }
    3591             : 
    3592           0 :         nSrcOffset += (nSrcStep - nBitCount);
    3593           0 :         nDstOffset += (nDstStep - nBitCount);
    3594             :     }
    3595             : }

    3949             : 
    3950             : /************************************************************************/
    3951             : /*                         BlockBasedRasterIO()                         */
    3952             : /*                                                                      */
    3953             : /*      This convenience function implements a dataset level            */
    3954             : /*      RasterIO() interface based on calling down to fetch blocks,     */
    3955             : /*      much like the GDALRasterBand::IRasterIO(), but it handles       */
    3956             : /*      all bands at once, so that a format driver that handles a       */
    3957             : /*      request for different bands of the same block efficiently       */
    3958             : /*      (i.e. without re-reading interleaved data) will efficiently.    */
    3959             : /*                                                                      */
    3960             : /*      This method is intended to be called by an overridden           */
    3961             : /*      IRasterIO() method in the driver specific GDALDataset           */
    3962             : /*      derived class.                                                  */
    3963             : /*                                                                      */
    3964             : /*      Default internal implementation of RasterIO() ... utilizes      */
    3965             : /*      the Block access methods to satisfy the request.  This would    */
    3966             : /*      normally only be overridden by formats with overviews.          */
    3967             : /*                                                                      */
    3968             : /*      To keep things relatively simple, this method does not          */
    3969             : /*      currently take advantage of some special cases addressed in     */
    3970             : /*      GDALRasterBand::IRasterIO(), so it is likely best to only       */
    3971             : /*      call it when you know it will help.  That is in cases where     */
    3972             : /*      data is at 1:1 to the buffer, and you know the driver is        */
    3973             : /*      implementing interleaved IO efficiently on a block by block     */
    3974             : /*      basis. Overviews will be used when possible.                    */
    3975             : /************************************************************************/
    3976             :

    4585             : /**
    4586             :  * \brief Copy all dataset raster data.
    4587             :  *
    4588             :  * This function copies the complete raster contents of one dataset to
    4589             :  * another similarly configured dataset.  The source and destination
    4590             :  * dataset must have the same number of bands, and the same width
    4591             :  * and height.  The bands do not have to have the same data type.
    4592             :  *
    4593             :  * This function is primarily intended to support implementation of
    4594             :  * driver specific CreateCopy() functions.  It implements efficient copying,
    4595             :  * in particular "chunking" the copy in substantial blocks and, if appropriate,
    4596             :  * performing the transfer in a pixel interleaved fashion.
    4597             :  *
    4598             :  * Currently the only papszOptions value supported are :
    4599             :  * <ul>
    4600             :  * <li>"INTERLEAVE=PIXEL/BAND" to force pixel (resp. band) interleaved read and
    4601             :  * write access pattern (this does not modify the layout of the destination
    4602             :  * data)</li> <li>"COMPRESSED=YES" to force alignment on target dataset block
    4603             :  * sizes to achieve best compression.</li> <li>"SKIP_HOLES=YES" to skip chunks
    4604             :  * for which GDALGetDataCoverageStatus() returns GDAL_DATA_COVERAGE_STATUS_EMPTY
    4605             :  * (GDAL &gt;= 2.2)</li>
